#######################
Unrenderable Composites
#######################

SAVVY: Vim generally does not render composite characters, but sometimes it will.
- Most composites will always appear as two symbols.
- Some composites will render if you Alt-tab away from Vim
  and then Alt-tab back, but will decompose into two separate
  characters as soon as you scroll (e.g., <PageUp>) or move the
  cursor to that line.
  - Composites that render when you switch apps away and back
    to Vim include:
    - Flags
    - Emoji with skin tones

============
country-flag
============

TRYME: Normally, Vim shows flag emoji as two bold letter-like
       characters, e.g., an ğŸ‡¦ and a ğŸ‡© for Andorra.
- But you can "trick" (coerce?) Vim to draw the composite character
  (in this case, the flag emoji), if you do one of two things:
  - You can place the cursor between the two decomposed characters,
    e.g., between the ğŸ‡¦ and the ğŸ‡©, and then move the cursor up or
    down one line; or
  - You alt-tab away from Vim and alt-tab back to Vim.
- However, once you you move the cursor to another position on a line
  that shows a composite, or if you page-up or page-down (or otherwise
  move the composite out of the view and then back into view again),
  the composite decomposes again into two separate characters.

CXREF: See Unicode thoughts on flag emoji, and controversies
       that arise by including them in the character set:
  https://blog.unicode.org/2022/03/the-past-and-future-of-flag-emoji.html

U+1F1E6 U+1F1E8  ğŸ‡¦ğŸ‡¨  flag: Ascension Island - flag

â”€ This file shows Unicode Version 15 â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
===========================================================================

The list above is based on Unicode v15.0:
- *[Unicode] Emoji Charts / Emoji List, v11.0*
  https://unicode.org/emoji/charts-15.0/emoji-list.html
Unicode v15.0 is the latest Unicode as of 2022-09-15.
- For the latest version, see:
  https://www.unicode.org/emoji/charts/emoji-list.html

===========================================================================
â”€ Install fonts with the latest Emoji characters â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
===========================================================================

Note that Vim's ``guifont`` setting does not supply the emoji glyphs.
Vim will pull emoji from whatever appropriate font you have installed
(under either ``/usr/share/fonts/`` or ``$HOME/.fonts``).
- So while the author prefers Hack font, augmented with Nerd Fonts::
    set guifont=Hack\ Nerd\ Font\ Mono\ 9
  (from: https://github.com/ryanoasis/nerd-fonts/releases)
  you'll need to find and install an appropriate emoji font,
  at least to see emoji from v12.0 and above (at least for my
  Linux Mint 19.3 machine, which has emoji up to v11.0 by
  default, I think).
- One option is JoyPixels, which, after supplying your email address
  and receiving a logon code, let's you download their font free for
  personal use:
    https://joypixels.com
  though as of this writing, 2022-09-15, JoyPixels 6.6 for Android
  (a TTF font, which you can install on Linux) includes Unicode v13.0
  emoji, but not v14.0 or v15.0.
- Another option is *Noto Emoji* fonts.
  - The release circa 2021-11-01 supports Unicode 14.0:
    https://github.com/googlefonts/noto-emoji
    https://github.com/googlefonts/noto-emoji/releases
  Simply download the archive, unpack it, copy the ``*.ttf`` files
  from the ``fonts/`` directory to your ``~/.fonts`` directory, and
  rebuild the font cache::
    sudo fc-cache -fv
  And Vim should immediately start showing v14.0 Unicode emoji
  (I've also seen Vim use the new emoji as soon as the TTF is
   copied to the fonts directory, without rebuilding cache).
  - Alternatively, you could probably download the TTF file directly from
    source:
      https://github.com/googlefonts/noto-emoji/tree/main/fonts
      https://github.com/googlefonts/noto-emoji/raw/main/fonts/NotoColorEmoji.ttf

===========================================================================
â”€ Setup Vim reStructuredText syntax highlights and folding  â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
===========================================================================

This emoji-lookup is highlighted correctly using the latest Vim syntax
file. E.g., if you build from sources, you might find it under home::
    ~/.local/share/vim/vim90/syntax/rst.vim
- With URL https://github.com/marshallward/vim-restructuredtext
  and *Latest Revision: 2020-03-31*.

You can enable Vim folding on the double-delimited reST headers in this
document with the reSTfold plugin:
  https://github.com/landonb/vim-reSTfold#ğŸ™
- Then press <F5> (or run ``:call ReSTFolderUpdateFolds(1)``)
  in this file to calculate fold boundaries and close all folds.
  - You can then use Vim's normal ``za`` to expand/collapse single
    sections, or ``zr`` to open folds one level, ``[z`` to move the
    cursor to the header, etc.

The author has additional reST syntax highlight projects that add
special highlights specifically for managing notes in your editor:
  https://github.com/landonb/vim-reST-highdefs#ğŸ¨
  https://github.com/landonb/vim-reST-highfive#ğŸ–
  https://github.com/landonb/vim-reST-highline#â–
- Hint: Install https://github.com/landonb/dubs_web_hatch
  to wire ``gW`` in Vim to opening the URL under the cursor.

===========================================================================
â”€ Vim does not typically render skin tone composites â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
===========================================================================

Skin-tone variations are not listed, because Vim does not render them well.
- See *Full Skin Tone List*
  https://unicode.org/emoji/charts-15.0/full-emoji-modifiers.html
- Vim usually decomposes composites into the two base emoji characters,
  e.g., if you scrolled to this section, you should see two symbols on
  each of the next two lines, a yellow waving hand and a skin tone square
  on each line (as two separate characters each, like this: ğŸ‘‹ ğŸ½):
    ğŸ‘‹ğŸ½
    ğŸ‘‹ğŸ¿
  (although if you're viewing this on GitHub, or in another editor, you
   might see the correct composites).
  - But note â€” and this is weird â€” if you alt-tab away from Vim and
    then alt-tab return, the skin tone composites will render correctly!
  - Or, if you put the cursor between the two composite characters, and
    then move the cursor up or down one line, they render composited.
  - However, if you move the cursor left-right through the composite, or
    if you page-up or page-down (or otherwise move the composite out view
    and then back into view again), the composite decomposes again.
    - [As seen on Vim v9.0 1-728 (Linux Mint MATE 19.3).]

-------

skin-tone

1141  U+1F3FB  ğŸ»  light skin tone
1142  U+1F3FC  ğŸ¼  medium-light skin tone
1143  U+1F3FD  ğŸ½  medium skin tone
1144  U+1F3FE  ğŸ¾  medium-dark skin tone
1145  U+1F3FF  ğŸ¿  dark skin tone

(note GitHub shows these as little â–¡ symbols and not as large color squares)

â”€ Unicode TOC & Legend â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
===========================================================================

TOC__: (for emoji above)::

  Smileys & Emotion
  People & Body
  Component
  Animals & Nature
  Food & Drink
  Travel & Places
  Activities
  Objects
  Symbols
  Flags

KEY__: Legend (for Unicode entries above)::

  Code-Point  The-Glyph  CLDR-Short-Name - Other | Keywords (Author's | Synonyms) âˆ¦ Variations

-------

KEY__: In the emojis above, keywords between parentheses were added
       by this author, to help search the file for emoji. The other
       keywords from copied the https://unicode.org source.

- CXREF: Check out this emoji thesaurus to help find a symbol for a word:

    https://emojicombos.com/

  - E.g., there's no "glue" emoji, but Emoji Combos suggests using,
    among other images, the adhesive bandage, or the lotion bottle,
    etc.:

      https://emojicombos.com/glue

-------

Note that the Variations are Variation Selector glyphs, and include 1, 2, or three glyphs:

- KEY__: The ``Variations`` after the ``âˆ¦`` label show variation sequences,
  and might be of one of the following formats:

  - Show all three variations::

      ... âˆ¦ VS15-Glyph Non-VS-Glyph VS16-Glyph

    e.g.,::

      U+1F600  ğŸ˜€  grinning face - grin âˆ¦ ğŸ˜€ï¸ ğŸ˜€ ğŸ˜€ï¸

  - Show two Variation Selector glyphs::

      ... âˆ¦ VS15-Glyph VS16-Glyph

    e.g.,::

      U+1F637  ğŸ˜·  face with medical mask - cold | doctor | sick âˆ¦ ğŸ˜·ï¸ ğŸ˜·ï¸

  - Show just the Variant Selector-15 glyph::

      ... âˆ¦ VS15-Glyph

    e.g.,::

      U+1F609  ğŸ˜‰  winking face - wink âˆ¦ ğŸ˜‰ï¸

    This format is useful when the VS-16 glyph is rendered same as the
    non-Variant form.

  - Note the leftmost glyph (*The-Glyph*) is not necessarily the
    non-Variant form, but might be whatever variant renders better
    in Vim (which is prone to clipping some variants if it doesn't
    allot the typical two columns for the character).

=========================================================================
â”€ Some Unicode are colorful (ğŸ¦…), but others absorb the foreground (ğŸ¿) â”€
=========================================================================

Not all Unicode render predictably.

Some Unicode are statically colored and will always appear the same, e.g.,::

  Colorful:  âœŠ ğŸ’¼ ğŸš€ ğŸ™‹ ğŸ° ğŸ”… ğŸ”† ğŸ’¨ ğŸ’¢ ğŸ’¥ ğŸ’ ğŸ¥’ ğŸ¥• ğŸ¦ ğŸ¦… ğŸ§ ğŸ¦˜ ğŸ­ ğŸ¬ ğŸš¢ ğŸ¦›  â›µ ğŸ¤¨ ğŸ˜¶ ğŸ¤¦ ğŸ¤·

But other Unicode will be colored according to the foreground color, e.g.,::

  Monocolor:
    fg_red () { printf "\033[31m"; }
    attr_reset () { printf "\033[0m"; }
    echo -e "$(fg_red) ğŸ›¡ âœ³ âœ´ â‡ ğŸ—£ â›°  ğŸ•Š ğŸ¿ â˜»  â˜º  $(attr_reset)"

(Though not the case on GitHub, where everything above renders colorfully.)

===========================================================================
â”€ U+FE0F Var Selector-16 Explained â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
===========================================================================

- *Variation Selector-16* (aka Var Selector-16, above) is U+FE0F,
  an invisible codepoint that specifies that the preceding character
  should be displayed with emoji presentation. It is only required if
  the preceding character defaults to text presentation.

    https://emojipedia.org/variation-selector-16/

  E.g., the eye character, U+1F441, is ğŸ‘. But with Variation
    Selector-16, U+1F441 U+FE0Fm, it's ğŸ‘ï¸.

KEY__: The ``âˆ¦`` label is used in the tables above to show variation sequences,
such as the VS15 and VS16 glyphs (Variation Selector-15 and Variation Selector-16),
or the base code point (if the glyph shown is already a variation) e.g.,::
  U+1F637  ğŸ˜·  face with medical mask - cold | doctor | face | face with medical mask | mask | sick âˆ¦ ğŸ˜·ï¸ ğŸ˜·ï¸
Note that Unicode.org (the glyph on the left) uses the code point with no
variation selector, e.g., U+1F637 (ğŸ˜·). The two glyphs on the left use the
variation selector, e.g., U+1F637 U+FE0E (ğŸ˜·ï¸), and  U+1F637 U+FE0F (ğŸ˜·ï¸).
- I tried to find a list of Variation Selector glyphs on Unicode.org, but
  I don't see any. So here are some other reference(s):
  https://www.ii.com/unicode-variation-selectors-15-16/
  https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Variant_form_(Unicode)
  - *Emoji Variations and Names (Emoji 11.0 / Unicode 11.0.0)*
    https://gist.github.com/janlelis/dd1ef0edfb06cedc5c19c8424ed9d5ee
  - *Emoji vs. Text Presentation*
    https://character.construction/emoji-vs-text

â”€ Braille Patterns â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

â”€ ASCII Spinners â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€

Footnote marker hierarchy: ``* â€  â€¡ Â§ â€– Â¶``
- ``*`` Asterisk/Star
- ``â€ `` Obelisk/Dagger/Obelus
- ``â€¡`` Double Dagger/Diesis
- ``Â§`` Section Sign
- ``â€–`` Translingual/Double Vertical Line
- ``Â¶`` Paragraph sign/blind P/pilcrow
Also possibly:
- ``#`` Number/Pound Sign / Hash/Hash mark / Hashtag / Hex / Octothorp/Octothorpe/Octathorp/Octatherp / Sharp
  - Not to be confused with the *Viewdata square* ``âŒ—``
  - Alternatively called (there are more?!): *crosshatch, crunch, fence, flash,
    garden fence, garden gate, gate, grid, hak, mesh, oof, pig-pen, punch mark,
    rake, scratch, scratch mark, tic-tac-toe, and unequal*
      https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Number_sign
- ``Î”`` Delta
- ``â—Š`` Lozenge/Diamond
- ``â†“`` Downwards Arrow
- ``â˜`` White Right Pointing Index

Complete footnote marker hierarchy: ``* â€  â€¡ Â§ â€– Â¶ # âŒ— â™¯ Î” â—Š â†“ â˜ ** â€ â€  â€¡â€¡ Â§Â§ â€–â€– Â¶Â¶ ## âŒ—âŒ— â™¯â™¯ Î”Î” â—Šâ—Š â†“â†“ â˜â˜``

- *The traditional order of these symbols in English is *, â€ , â€¡, Â§, â€–, Â¶.*
  â€ ::
    Robert Bringhurst (2005). The Elements of Typographic Style (version 3.1). Point
    Roberts, Wash.: Hartley and Marks. pp 68â€“69. Bringhurst goes on to say â€œBut beyond
    the ... double dagger, this order is not familiar to most readers, and never was.â€
  https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Note_(typography)

  - But because reST formatting, you'll likely want to skip ``*`` and start with ``â€ ``.

- If you need more symbols:
  - You can try doubling the same marks:
    - ``** â€ â€  â€¡â€¡ Â§Â§ â€–â€– Â¶Â¶``
    https://www.editage.com/insights/footnotes-in-tables-part-1-choice-of-footnote-markers-and-their-sequence
  - Or you could reach further into the symbols hat, e.g.:
      - "Other symbols, including the ``# Î” â—Š â†“ â˜``, have also been used."
        https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Note_(typography)#cite_note-2::
            Â¹â° Hasler, â€œA Show of Hands,â€ 4. The standard sequence of â€œreference marksâ€
            was *, â€ , [double-dagger], Â§, ||, Â¶, and â˜ (ğŸ‘‰).
          http://www.livesandletters.ac.uk/papers/FOR_2005_04_001.pdf
        https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Note_(typography)#cite_note-3
          See usage in John Bach McMaster's *History of the People of the United States*.
          https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Bach_McMaster

- (This text has since been removed: "used to be some funky Unicode keywords
   here, but it broke the npm website on chrome, so they were removed, sorry")
- I'm not sure what character set this is, and I haven't seen them on any
  Unicode table online (and I haven't dug any deeper than that, but I
  appreciate how someone cobbled together readable English! And so dark).
- See also the project page and a blog post about the project
  https://github.com/npm/dezalgo
  https://blog.izs.me/2013/08/designing-apis-for-asynchrony

  *ThÍe DaÒ‰rk PoÅ„y LoÍ˜rÍ d HE ÌCÍ¡OMÌ´EÌ¸S*::

- The ``please`` shell fcn invokes the spirit of *dezalgo* for its error msg::
    ã€…sÍ‰Í“Ì˜á»¶sÍŸÍ…Í‰Ì©Ì©TÌ¯Í…ÌªeÍ˜Ì˜ÌºÌ°Ì™MÌ¬Ì¼ EÌ†Ì½Ì¿ÌŠÍ¥ÌÍ«Ì–Ì¤Í”Í”ÌŸÌ¹rÍ˜Ì Ì¼Ì¯Ì¹Í…Ì¦Ì¦rÌ£Ì˜Ì¬Í”Ì™Í‡Ì OÌÌšÌ¶Ì­Í“rÌ§ÍšÌœÍ“Ì°Ì­Ì­ã… TÌ•Í–Ì®hÍ–aÌ›Í…tÍ€Í–Ì£Í‰ WÌ¶Ì¥Ì£Í–Ì¦oÍ¡Ì–Ì«uÌ•Ì¼Ì¦Í”Ì¥Ì®lÍ¢ÌºÌ±Í–Ì¯Í“Í™ÍˆdÌ·Ì²Ì¦Ì–Í“ iÌ°Ì®Ì©nÌ¶Ì³Í™Ì«ÍvÍÍ‰okÌ­Ì¬ÌÍ…eÍÌÍÌ©Ì«ÍÌ© cÌ™Í‰hÌ•ÌÍ”Í…Ì©Ì™aÌ²Í–Ì»Ì—Ì¹oÌ¥Ì¼Ì«sÌÌ–ÌœÌÍšÌ«ÌŸ aÌ›Í…nÌªÌ¯ÍˆdÍ dÌ´Ì°Í“Ì»Ì£Ì®Í…Í•iÍ˜Ì–Í“Í”Ì®Ì±Ì»sÌ§Í”Ì¯Ì©oÍ€rÍÌ¹Ì°Ì–Í‰ÍˆdÌ·Ì²Ì¦Ì–Í“eÌ²Í“Ì r"

Unicode Whitespace
https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Whitespace_character

*Space characters and â€œzero-width spacesâ€ in Unicode* table from:
  http://jkorpela.fi/chars/spaces.html

- Hint: Copy the space you desire from between the 'foo' and 'bar' pairs.

Code    Name of the character             Sample    Width of the character
======  ===============================   =======   =================================================
U+0020  SPACE                             foo bar   Depends on font, typically 1/4 em, often adjusted
U+00A0  NO-BREAK SPACE (nbsp)             foo bar   As a space, but often not adjusted
U+1680  OGHAM SPACE MARK                  fooáš€bar   Unspecified; usually not really a space but a dash
U+180E  MONGOLIAN VOWEL SEPARATOR         fooá bar	0
U+2000  EN QUAD                           fooâ€€bar   1 en (= 1/2 em)
U+2001  EM QUAD                           fooâ€bar   1 em (nominally, the height of the font)
U+2002  EN SPACE (nut)                    fooâ€‚bar   1 en (= 1/2 em)                             [Digraph: 1N]
U+2003  EM SPACE (mutton)                 fooâ€ƒbar   1 em                                        [Digraph: 1M]
U+2004  THREE-PER-EM SPACE (thick space)  fooâ€„bar   1/3 em                                      [Digraph: 3M]
U+2005  FOUR-PER-EM SPACE (mid space)     fooâ€…bar   1/4 em                                      [Digraph: 4M]
U+2006  SIX-PER-EM SPACE                  fooâ€†bar   1/6 em                                      [Digraph: 6M]
U+2007  FIGURE SPACE                      fooâ€‡bar   â€œTabular widthâ€, the width of digits
U+2008  PUNCTUATION SPACE                 fooâ€ˆbar   The width of a period â€œ.â€
U+2009  THIN SPACE                        fooâ€‰bar   1/5 em (or sometimes 1/6 em)                [Digraph: 1T]
U+200A  HAIR SPACE                        fooâ€Šbar   Narrower than THIN SPACE                    [Digraph: 1H]
U+200B  ZERO WIDTH SPACE                  fooâ€‹bar  0
U+202F  NARROW NO-BREAK SPACE             fooâ€¯bar   Narrower than NO-BREAK SPACE (or SPACE),
                                            â€œtypically the width of a thin space or a mid spaceâ€
U+205F  MEDIUM MATHEMATICAL SPACE         fooâŸbar   4/18 em
U+3000  IDEOGRAPHIC SPACE                 fooã€€bar  The width of ideographic (CJK) characters.  [Digraph: IS]
U+FEFF  ZERO WIDTH NO-BREAK SPACE         fooï»¿bar  0

USAGE:
- I have used these to pad a Vim ``titlestring`` so that it maintains
  the same width when it's displaying slightly different information:
    https://github.com/landonb/vim-title-bar-time-of-day
- The mutton ``â€ƒ`` (``<CTRL-K>1M``) is an em space that looks like a
  space but that won't be identified as a ``[:space:]``.
  - This could be useful if you use leading spaces in a reSTfold header
      https://github.com/landonb/vim-reSTfold#ğŸ™
    E.g.,::
      #######################################################
      â€ƒâ€ƒâ€ƒâ† 3 em spaces cause ``\\#`` to over/underline prefix
      #######################################################
      .. HINT: Try it: Put cursor in title and type ``\\+``
- Other than that, it's a very fixed-width world for a dev, so I'd be
  curious to include other tricks people have for Unicode whitespace.
